<div class="row result"><div class="col-sm-3 result_headword"><h3 headword_id="29104">1 is</h3><span class="citation">Cite this: eDIL s.v. 1 is or <a class="reference" href="29104">dil.ie/29104</a></span><br/><span class="revision">Last Revised:
                2019</span><br/><p style="margin-top: 4px" class="small">Forms:
                nídam, nída, atar, atin, ammi, bem, be, combin, is, am, im, isam, isim, sam, isam, am, isam, nidha, nis, indat, n-iat, cenita, coich, citné, cisné, cis, manid, minad, minid, munid, minap, munab, béso, bésu, gon, gion, indid, inid, inad, ina, 'nar, díand, díanid, díanad, dían, díanda, dían(d)at, dána, dán, darab, bad, ba, ba, badat, ba, -bo, -p, -b, cid, -rop, -rup, -rub, ropond, ce, cía, cit, cía, ce, bed, bad, pad, bud, ba-da-, bádam, ma, matis, diambtís, bé, biam, bum, bid, bith, beith, bed, bud, -pa, -ba, nípa-dn-aidrech, -ba, -pa, -bo, -po, -bu, -pu, -b, -bad, -bud, bit, be(i)t, bat, biat, bidat, -rsam, -rbam, -bi, ropsa, rupsa, ropsat, robsat, ropat, robat, ropot, ropdat, -rbsat, -rsat, -rsa, -rbat, nārsat, ba, bu, bo, be, fa, fá, fo, bad, bud, ba-id-n-, fa, fá, -pu, -bu, -po, -bo, -p, nip, nipu, -rbu, -rpu, -rpo, -rbo, rba, -rob, -rb, -ra, -r, -rsa(t), -rso, -rsa, -rsad, rsam, -rsat, -rbtar, -rptar, -rtar, -rbat, -rpsat, -rsat, -psat, -bsat, -psatar, gomsad</p></div><div class="col-sm-9 result_content">
   
    <p class="result">
      <span class="pos v" style="color: #ff8000">v</span> 
      <span class="pos copula" style="color: #ff8000">copula</span> (see Strachan, Substantive Verb in O.Ir. Glosses 
(
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Phil.Soc.Trans." title="eDIL Bibliography">Phil. Soc. Trans.</strong></span> 1899
      ); Ó Máille, Verbs of Existence in 
Irish; Dillon, Nominal Predicates in Irish (
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/ZCP" title="eDIL Bibliography">ZCP</strong></span> xvi
      , 
        xvii
      ) ; 

        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/GOI" title="eDIL Bibliography">GOI</strong></span> § 814 ff.
      ; Ó Nolan Studies in Mod. Ir.).</p>
   
    <p class="result"> 
USAGE.</p>
   
    <p class="result"> 
The copula is alway unstressed and proclitic. The 
normal order of words is vb.+pred.+subj., <span class="lbl">e.g.</span> 
        is cele dae 
in fer hisin, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 30c3
        
      . is bésad inna flatho doem <span class="frn ">et</span> dofich 
(<span class="lbl">i.e.</span> to protect and to avenge is a princely custom), 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 
9d2
      . Prec. by asyntactic nom.: 
        fáilte cáich bad fáilte 
dúib-si, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 5d24
        
      . mad i n-aeclis tra in choss is hé óis 
achtáil `<span class="quote">if then it be in the church, the foot is the practical 
folk</span>,' 
        12a23
      . Frequ. in verse: 
        Illand mac Scanlain is marb, 

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Anecd." title="eDIL Bibliography">Anecd.</strong></span> i 12.24
        
      . 
        andar la fer bis a cein | Inber Cindbera 
is reid, 
          15.1
        
      . 
        a comrádh bind nocho brég, 
          35 § 81.
        
       An 
inversion of the usual order (see Ó Máille, <span class="lbl">op. cit.</span> p. 74) 
occurs in: nī bu ṡanctBrigit ṡúanach (<span class="lbl">v.l.</span> sanctbrigit 
suanach) `<span class="quote">Saint B. was not drowsy</span>,' 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Hy." title="eDIL Bibliography">Hy.</strong></span> v 21
       (see 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/GOI" title="eDIL Bibliography">GOI</strong></span> p. 476
       and 
        n. 168
      ). 
        is tria chin mban | bit 
fernai fer dlochtai, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/LU" title="eDIL Bibliography">LU</strong></span> 8430
        
       (FB, rhetoric). Common in 
rel. sentences in Fél.: mórṡlúag A. | dia mbu Demon 
dubach `<span class="quote">from whom the Devil was sorrowful</span>,' 
      
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/F&#xE9;l." title="eDIL Bibliography">Fél.</strong></span> April 2
      . 
        súi 
diand Ériu inmall, 
          Sept. 10.
        
       manach | asa díthrub dubach 
`<span class="quote">whose hermitage is gloomy</span>,' 
        Prol. 98
       (but: 
        S. | ata soilsi 
slechtae, 
          Sept. 7.
        
       
        Carissim ... | asa rúamdae relic, 
          Ap. 16
        
      ). 
Where the predicate is a compound phrase the subject is 
introduced into the middle of it (Strachan, <span class="lbl">op. cit.</span> p. 49.30), 
<span class="lbl">e.g.</span> 
        is irlam ind anim do thuil Dée, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 5c18
        
      . 
        nirbu samlaid 
són doibsom, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 90c27
        
      . 
        nibo mór a mbríg linn, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 18d10
        
      .</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
In O.Ir. when the subject of the copula was a personal 
pronoun it was, as in other verbs, implicit in the verbal 
form: 
        am irlam, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 13c8
        
      . 
        at fechem dom, 
          32a21
        
      . combed 
<span class="frn ">adultera</span>
       `<span class="quote">so that she should be a.</span>', 
        3c9
      . nirbu choimdiu 
`<span class="quote">he had not been a lord</span>,' 
        33a5
      . bad carthi `<span class="quote">let him be loved</span>,' 

        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Sg." title="eDIL Bibliography">Sg.</strong></span> 148a2
      . nítat ainmnidi `<span class="quote">they are not nominatives</span>,' 
        189a10
      . 

        amal bemmis bibdaid, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 114d4
        
      . It was frequently 
strengthened by a pronominal particle suffixed to the 
pred. not necessarily to express emphasis, nor to distinguish 
between persons: niba dimicthe-se libsi `<span class="quote">I should not be 
despised by you</span>,' 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 21d3
       (but: nida apstal apstil `<span class="quote">I am 
not an apostle's apostle</span>,' 
        18c1
      ). 
        massu rath-som, 
          5a30
        
      . 

        ciasu i colinn am béo-sa, 
          19a20
        
      . 
        it firian-su, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 55d11
        
      . 

        ammi cland-ni doib-som, 
          101d9
        
      . 
        ropsa huallach-sa, 
          49b12
        
       
(<span class="lbl">cf.</span> 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/GOI" title="eDIL Bibliography">GOI</strong></span> § 811
      ). 
        nimda scál-sa ┐ nimda aurdrach, 

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/ZCP" title="eDIL Bibliography">ZCP</strong></span> xiii 373.11
        
      .</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
The logical pred. of the copula may be (a) an adjective ; 
(b) a prepositional phrase; (c) an adverb; (d) a pronoun ; 
(e) the substantival demonstrative í; (f) the subject of a 
relative verb; (g) a clause introduced by as n- `<span class="quote">that it is</span>' ; 
(h) a substantive.</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
At all periods of the language the predicates (a), (b), 
(c) and (d) immediately followed the copula.</p>
   
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">a</span>) In O.Ir. the general rule was that the predicative 
adj. agreed with the subj. of the copula in gender and 
number (see Dillon, <span class="lbl">op. cit.</span>, for development from O.Ir., 
of which he cites as type: 
          it moírb in boill sin, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 11d11
          
        , 
to Mod. Ir.: 
          is mór iatt, is saidhbir na tírtha so, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Maund." title="eDIL Bibliography">Maund.</strong></span> 
§ 138
          
        , 
          §227
        ).</p>
    
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">b</span>) 
          amal as o spirut, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 15b7
          
        . 
          ciaba beo bid do precept 
anme Crist, 
            23b29
          
        . 
          is occ maid atáa, 
            6a18
          
        . 
          condib tria 
n-uile mbethaid ón, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Tur." title="eDIL Bibliography">Tur.</strong></span> 71.
          
         
          is fria binn aníar atá t'esérge, 

            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Thes." title="eDIL Bibliography">Thes.</strong></span> ii 242.3
          
         (Ardm.). 
          is airi asbersom ..., 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 126c10
          
        . 

          cid tre étged rop othar, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Cr&#xED;thG." title="eDIL Bibliography">Críth G.</strong></span> 61.
          
         
          nochon ara omun 
cena, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TBC-I1" title="eDIL Bibliography">TBC-I¹</strong></span> 2364.
          
         
          gonadh uime sin adeir I.<span class="oRef">¤</span> ..., 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TSh." title="eDIL Bibliography">TSh.</strong></span> 4816.
          
        
      </p>
    
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">c</span>) 
          níp and nob irpaid, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 8b2
          
        . 
          hóre is amne atáa, 

            12d7
          
        . 
          is samlith is comadas dúun ..., 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Thes." title="eDIL Bibliography">Thes.</strong></span> ii 246.3
          
         (Cam.).</p>
    
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">d</span>) 
          mad hé á luum, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 4a14
          
        . bad hé for n-ere `<span class="quote">let 
Him be your burden</span>,' 
          9d12
        . 
          rupu sí a rreilic, 
            33a22
          
        . 
          is tú 
is diliu limsa diib, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/IT" title="eDIL Bibliography">IT</strong></span> iii 83 § 69.
          
         
          ionnus gomadh é féin bud 
ughdar réna bheathaidh, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TSh." title="eDIL Bibliography">TSh.</strong></span> 3406.
          
        
      </p>
    
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
When the logical predicate of the copula was either (e) 
the substantival demonstrative í or (f) the antecedent of 
a relative verb, or (g) a clause introduced by as n- `<span class="quote">that it 
is</span>' a pronoun was introduced immediately after the copula 
to act as grammatical predicate while the logical predicate 
stood in apposition to this pronoun.</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">e</span>) 
        matu hé ata horpamin indí rochomalnisset recht, 

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 2c14
        
      . 
        bit hé magistir dongegat indhí asindisset a 
tola féisne dóib, 
          30d8
        
      . 
        it hé in toirthi amal sodin inna hí 
adfiadatar hi testimnib file isint salm anuas, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 46c14
        
      .</p>
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">f</span>) is hé didiu in tecttaire maith condaig indocbáil dia 
thigerni <span class="ediltr">the good envoy is he who seeks his lord's glory</span>, 

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 8d20
        . 
          it hé <span class="frn ">inimici</span> lessom <span class="frn ">qui fraudant et qui iniuriam 
faciunt</span>
          , 
            9c25
          
        . it hé gními epscuip asmbeir sís <span class="ediltr">the works 
of a bishop are the things he mentions below</span>, 
          28b20
        . is he in 
firfindbathach no in firion atcobra na huile <span class="frn ">beatusa</span>
         <span class="ediltr">the 
truly blessed ... is he who desires all the blessings</span>, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Hib.Min." title="eDIL Bibliography">Hib. Min.</strong></span> 
429.
        
      </p>
    
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">g</span>) 
          is ed asberat ind heretic as laigiu deacht maicc indaas 
deacht athar, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 17c7
          
        . ni ed a met as n-etarcnad dun 
`<span class="quote">not only that it is known to us</span>,' 
          138a12
        . 
          is ed asberat as 
ndu deacht ... rogabad in salm so, 
            24d29
          
        . 
          is ed adfet a 
legend as ndath glas roboi forsind sléib fo chosmailius 
saphirr, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 84d4
          
        .</p>
    
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
(<span class="edilb">h</span>) With indef. noun as pred.: 
          condib dídnad domsa 
foirbthetu hirisse dúibsi, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 1b1
          
        . 
          combad notire rod-scribad cosse, 
            27d16
          
        . 
          mástat carait ... mastat námait, 

            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/LU" title="eDIL Bibliography">LU</strong></span> 9090
          
        -
          1
        . 
          níor ghníomh meirbh, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/DD&#xE1;na" title="eDIL Bibliography">DDána</strong></span> 91 § 24.
          
        
      </p>
    
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
With def. noun as pred.: in O.Ir. and early Mid. Ir. a 
definite substantive can immediately follow the copula. 
Even in O.Ir. however a pronoun is frequently introduced 
immediately after the copula as grammatical predicate, 
the logical predicate standing in apposition (<span class="lbl">cf.</span> (e), (f) and 
(g) above). This is the normal construction in the later 
language: ni a doenacht fesine ru-da-n-ordan `<span class="quote">not his 
own Manhood has dignified Him</span>,' 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 33c5
      . 
        ni in cholinn 
donatháira acht is a n-accobor, 
          3d3
        
      . is athir-som innaní 
techte foirbthetith `<span class="quote">he is the father of them that possess 
perfection</span>,' 
        2c11
      . 
        mad Ānlūan no-beth is'taig, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/ScM." title="eDIL Bibliography">ScM.</strong></span> 
§ 16.8
        
      . 
        is Duid a oenar rochachain inna psalmu, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Hib.Min." title="eDIL Bibliography">Hib. Min.</strong></span> 
134.
        
      
    </p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
With pronoun: 
        bit hé na precepta cétni no pridchob 
doib, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 17b20
        
      . 
        is hed a trede sin foloing, 
          29d17
        
      . 
        is hé 
in peccad rogéni a n-uile comaccobor, 
          3c25
        
      .</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
After the introduction of the pronoun, the normal order 
of the sentence seems to be that in which the predicate 
follows the pronoun but this order does not appear to be 
fixed and the predicate may be put at the end either for 
emphasis or for the better balance of the sentence, <span class="lbl">e.g.</span> a 
predicate which is the antecedent of a relative verb is 
most usually placed after the subject. Predicate and subject can only be distinguished by means of the context and 
the distinction, it would seem, is by no means as clear-cut 
in Irish as in other languages.</p>
   
    <p class="result"> 
Predicate immediately following pronoun: 
        ní ceilsom 
tra as n-é Crist in lie, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 4d16
        
      . 
        issí ind ainim as airlam do 
chomalnad recto Dé ní in corpp, 
          3d11
        
      . 
        measaim gurab é 
an bás, an marcach úd, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TSh." title="eDIL Bibliography">TSh.</strong></span> 37.
        
      
    </p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
Subject following pronoun: mate nama anfolaid in cele 
falla frithgnama `<span class="quote">if neglect of service was the only disqualification of the tenant</span>,' 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Laws" title="eDIL Bibliography">Laws</strong></span> ii 324.6
      . 
        ar is he besad felsub 
etarcert di dúlib <span class="frn ">et</span> saigid forru <span class="frn ">et</span> nebchretem a n-adiadar di 
crist, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 27a10
        
      . 
        it he <span class="frn ">caeli</span> la suide ind apstail soscelae, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 
42b7
        
      . 
        is ed mind n-aingel Crist mac Dé, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/LU" title="eDIL Bibliography">LU</strong></span> 944.
        
       
        measaim 
... gurab í an chathair úd Ierusalem an domhan, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TSh." title="eDIL Bibliography">TSh.</strong></span> 708.
        
      
    </p>
  
  
    
      <p class="result"> 
In O.Ir. where the subject of the copula was a pronoun 
of the 1st or 2nd person, it required no other expression 
with an indef. pred. than that supplied by the 1st or 2nd 
person of the copula: 
          at macc ríg, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Trip.2" title="eDIL Bibliography">Trip.²</strong></span> 970.
          
         
          itib ingena 
ríg talman, 
            1138
          
        . 
          am dún díthogail, 
            <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/IT" title="eDIL Bibliography">IT</strong></span> iii 53.26
          
        .</p>
    
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
<span class="lbl">Cf.</span> Mid. Ir.: 
        is descipul ... tu-su, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/PH" title="eDIL Bibliography">PH</strong></span> 2768.
        
       
        conid mog 
De thú, 
          510
        
      . 
        is gadaige thu, 
          7781
        
      . 
        is clann én athar ┐ 
én máthar sind, 
          7501
        
      .</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
With def. pred. the usage in O.Ir. is not certain (? at 
lūam in gaiscid grind (but: <span class="lbl">v.l.</span> at tualaing gaiscid grind), 

        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Bruchst." title="eDIL Bibliography">Bruchst.</strong></span> 12 § 20
      ). In the saga literature the normal expression is: 
        Setanta ... atomchomnaicse, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/LU" title="eDIL Bibliography">LU</strong></span> 4892.
        
       
        Rí 
Alban atomchomnaicse, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/RC" title="eDIL Bibliography">RC</strong></span> xiii 446 § 31.
        
      
    </p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
<span class="lbl">Cf.</span> Mid. Ir.: 
        is me Oengus céle Dé, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/SR" title="eDIL Bibliography">SR</strong></span> 8009.

          2876

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/PH" title="eDIL Bibliography">PH</strong></span> 3732.

       (but <span class="lbl">cf.</span> 
        Tuan mac Cairill mesi,

      ).</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
At all periods of the language the expression of the 
copula in the 3rd persons was not obligatory at the head of 
a principal sentence: 
        alind á óiph in forcitil, nemnech

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 7c1

      ).

    <p class="result"> 
SPECIAL USES.</p>
   
    <p class="result"> 
In periphrasis (see Strachan, <span class="lbl">op. cit.</span> p. 49): nitat huili 
robtar uilcc <span class="frn ">filii Israhel</span>
       `<span class="quote">all f. I. have not been evil</span>,' 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 
11a23
      . 
        is do immarchor chóre dotíagat ind fir so, 
          5a5
        
      .</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
Elliptical: demes .i. mess dēde and, ūair it dá scín lais 
<span class="ediltr">there are two blades ...</span>, 
        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Corm.Y" title="eDIL Bibliography">Corm. Y</strong></span> 438.

          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/MacCongl." title="eDIL Bibliography">MacCongl.</strong></span> 19.4
        
      .</p>
  
  
    <p class="result">

        <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/C&#xF3;icCon." title="eDIL Bibliography">Cóic Con.</strong></span> RE § 13.106
      .</p>

    <p class="result"> 
FORMS</p>
   
    <p class="result">(a) from O. Ir. glosses and texts in Thes. Pal. (for 
further exx. from O. Ir. glosses see Strachan, <span class="lbl">loc. cit.</span>). 
(b) from other texts.</p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
In Mid. Ir. the forms of the copula in the 1st and 2nd sg. 
and in all persons of the pl. fell to a great extent into disuse, 
their place being taken by the 3rd sg., of the tense required 
with a pron., corresponding in form to the O.Ir. infixed 
pron. or to the poss. pron. of the person and number to be 
expressed, infixed between it and the following predicate. 
Occasionally the inf. pron. was added to forms other than 
<span class="number sg.">sg.</span> <span class="per 3">3</span>, <span class="lbl">e.g.</span> nídam for nída (<span class="number s.">s.</span> <span class="per 1">1</span>), atar, atin (<span class="number pl.">pl.</span> <span class="per 3">3</span>+ inf. pron. 
<span class="number pl.">pl.</span> <span class="per 1">1</span>) for ammi, bem for be (<span class="tns fut.">fut.</span> <span class="number s.">s.</span> <span class="per 1">1</span>). These forms while 
at first used impersonally as already occurred in O. Ir., 
<span class="lbl">e.g.</span> 
        issum ēcen, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 10d24
        
      , 
        isat dílmain-siu, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 55d21
        
      , 

        diandam thísed mucc ḟonaithe robad-am béo, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Storiesfr.T&#xE1;in" title="eDIL Bibliography">Stories from Táin</strong></span> 5.16
        
      , later came to be felt as simply the copula, as is 
shown when plural forms are folld. by pl. adjj., <span class="lbl">e.g.</span> 
        nibar 
troig, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/SR" title="eDIL Bibliography">SR</strong></span> 3641
        
      , 
        gurdar síthaig, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Hib.Min." title="eDIL Bibliography">Hib. Min.</strong></span> 82.23
        
      , 
        acht co 
mbadar maithe díblínaib, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TBC-LL1" title="eDIL Bibliography">TBC-LL¹</strong></span> 35
        
      ; and by such instances 
as: 
        gidar comaltai, 
          <span class="lbl">ib.</span> 3680
        
      . 
        ropdhar fir chomdeirgide, 

          <span class="lbl">ib.</span> 3535
        
      . As it is not always possible to discover whether 
a particular writer regarded this combination of copula + inf. 
pron. as such or as copula only, all such examples have 
been grouped together, so that, for instance, all the forms 
under subj. past s. 1 below should be taken not necessarily 
as being, to the mind of the writer, that particular form 
but rather as being his way of expressing what would in 
O. Ir. be expressed by combin, <span class="lbl">etc.</span> </p>
  
  
    <p class="result"> 
Examples of the 1st and 2nd persons are found both in Classical verse and in Early Mod. Ir. prose but the more commonly occurring forms are those of the 
<span class="per 3">3</span>rd <span class="number sg.">sg.</span>, number and person being expressed by independent 
pronouns: 
        
          is ort iarraim gidh óg thú, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/DD&#xE1;na" title="eDIL Bibliography">DDána</strong></span> 67 § 3.
        
       
        is 
fearr mé iná thú, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/IGT" title="eDIL Bibliography">IGT</strong></span> Introd. 22 § 90.
        
       
        t'fhearg, a rí, ... | 
re searg dí bu fhearr inn-ne, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/DD&#xE1;na" title="eDIL Bibliography">DDána</strong></span> 10 § 22.
        
       
        ag an druing 
... rénar milis briathra borba, 
          <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/TSh." title="eDIL Bibliography">TSh.</strong></span> 1568.
        
       
        do bhríogh nach 
cumhachtach sinn féin ris aní se, 
          30
        
      . 
        is beannuighthe 
sibhse, 
          5669
        
      . 
        do bhríogh gurbh fheasach thú gurbh amadán 
mé, 
          9638
        
      .</p>

          <p class="result">Interrogative sentences containing cía, 
cid <span class="trans">
              <span class="def">who</span>, <span class="def">what</span> (<span class="def">is</span>)</span>. <span class="lbl">etc.</span>

              <span class="number pl.">pl.</span> <span class="per 3">3</span> citné (`<span class="quote">gekürzt aus <span class="frn ">ci ata n-é</span>
              </span>,' Thurn., 
                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/ZCP" title="eDIL Bibliography">ZCP</strong></span> xx 
372
              ): assindet sunt tra citné cumacte diandid cóir in 
fognam `<span class="quote">what are the powers unto which the service is proper</span>,' 

                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 6a9
              . citné briathra robatar `<span class="quote">what were the words</span> ?,' 

                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 61b7
              . citné robatar `<span class="quote">what were they</span>,' 
                <span class="lbl">ib.</span> 8
              . 
                citne a 
nanmand na soerbard (caidet, <span class="lbl">v.l.</span>), 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/IT" title="eDIL Bibliography">IT</strong></span> iii 5.8
                
              . 
                ceitni 
trī seōit fūair C. ?, 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/ZCP" title="eDIL Bibliography">ZCP</strong></span> xiii 5 § 19.
                
               
                citni rig ... robatar' sind 
amsir sin ?, 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/SR" title="eDIL Bibliography">SR</strong></span> 2347.
                
               The corresponding form in the Laws 
is cisné: cisne lesa do na ibh sen tascnat treise `<span class="quote">what cases 
of these extend to three days</span> ?,' 
                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Laws" title="eDIL Bibliography">Laws</strong></span> i 230.21
              . 
                cisne tri 
biada na tuillead leaptha na hapta, 
                  v 438.14
                
              . cisne trí 
ana soitcedach `<span class="quote">what are the three wealths</span> ...,' 
                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Triads" title="eDIL Bibliography">Triads</strong></span> 239.
               
Sometimes cis immediately precedes the noun : 
                cis formmenn écndaircc doslíat dílsi ?, 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/ZCP" title="eDIL Bibliography">ZCP</strong></span> xii 366.25
                
              . 
                cis ndíthle 
do trebaib na tuillet dire ?, 
                  26
                
              . 
                cis forcsen fola la Fēne ?, 

                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/BCr&#xF3;lige" title="eDIL Bibliography">BCrólige</strong></span> § 65.
                
               cis lir <span class="trans">
                <span class="def">how many</span>:</span> 
                cis lir congellait for tresi, 

                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Laws" title="eDIL Bibliography">Laws</strong></span> i 230.3
                
              . 
                cis lir lanamna docuisin la feine ?, 
                  ii 344.1
                
              . 

                cis lir chuir dochuisin ?, 
                  iii 4.5
                
              . 
                cis lir fodlai filet forsin 
mbairdne ?, 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/IT" title="eDIL Bibliography">IT</strong></span> iii 6.13
                
              . <span class="lbl">cf.</span> 
                cit lir fodlai ..., 
                  <span class="lbl">ib.</span> 20
                
              .</p>

              <p class="result">The form arimp in the Glosses

          <p class="result"> 
The form robo, robu and with inf. pron. rodbo, rodbu 
occurs in the sense <span class="trans">
              <span class="def">either, or</span>
            </span> (<span class="lbl">cf.</span> Fr. <span class="frn ">soit ... soit</span>). The editors 
of 
              <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Thes." title="eDIL Bibliography">Thes.</strong></span> Pal. (i 433 n.
            ) say it `<span class="quote">seems to be regular in the 
first of two or more alternatives.</span>' It is so used in the great 
majority of cases but in 
              <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 14c24
             and 
              <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 58b11
             (see 
below) it precedes the second alternative. Pedersen (
              <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/KZ" title="eDIL Bibliography">KZ</strong></span> 
xxxv 404 f
            . <span class="lbl">q.v.</span>) suggests an original meaning `<span class="quote">was es sei</span>' 
and the loss of the demonstrative pronoun a n- or aní before 
robo. Thurneysen (
              <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/GOI" title="eDIL Bibliography">GOI</strong></span> § 886
            ) believes it to have been a 
potential ro- subj. It is found somet. where in the Lat. 
<span class="frn ">uel .. uel</span> .., or Lat. <span class="frn ">aut .. aut</span> ... occur:</p>
         
          
            <p class="result">(<span class="edilb">a</span>) rodbo dia adroni 
... ł. is hé-som adroni ... <span class="ediltr">either God has committed</span> ..., 
                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 
29d29
              . 
                16d7
              . fo chenéle lugi [i]ssiu rodbo chosmi[liu]s 
`<span class="quote">as a kind of oath ... or a similitude</span>,' 
                14c24
              . robo intí forchain gl. siue qui docet, 
                5d10
              . 
                robo folad diles ł. doacaldmach, 

                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Sg." title="eDIL Bibliography">Sg.</strong></span> 197a1
                
              . 
                200b6
              . robu óenlitrib gl. uel singulis literis, 

                28a12
              . robu cho adersetar gl. uel emendentur ... (<span class="frn ">uel</span> ...), 
                <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span>

              . robu a caratrad gl. (uel necessitudo) uel (familiaritas), 

                58b11
               (but Eds. suggest on

            <p class="result">(<span class="edilb">iii</span>)</p>
           
            
              <p class="result">(<span class="edilb">a</span>) bid (this form, which Thurn. (
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/GOI" title="eDIL Bibliography">GOI</strong></span> § 806
                ) 
suggests may be an unstressed form of vn. buith, occurs 
regularly after amal, oldaas, is cumme, in doich, in comparative and equative clauses and in a few other instances. 
This would suit an ex. like 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Thes." title="eDIL Bibliography">Thes.</strong></span> ii 294 § 3
                 below but does 
not explain phrases where bid follow amal, is cumme, <span class="lbl">etc.</span> 
It survives into Mid. Ir. but is somet. replaced by bed or bad, 
and in a few cases spreads to other types of sentence (amal 
bid is regularly folld. by acc. <span class="lbl">cf.</span> mainbad, above): amal 
bid dia <span class="ediltr">as though he were God</span>, 
                  <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 26a7
                . 
                  amal bid claind 
noclantis, 
                    <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 63b9
                  
                . 
                  amail bith ball di crist, 
                    <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Thes." title="eDIL Bibliography">Thes.</strong></span> ii 255.14
                  
                 
(Stowe M.). 
                  amal fid na derscaigthiu, 
                    <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Ml." title="eDIL Bibliography">Ml.</strong></span> 37b22
                  
                . 
                  amal 
bid inn accaldim deithidnig (<span class="lbl">leg.</span> nd.), 
                    35c27
                  
                . 
                  is cumme 
doib bid idalte domeltis, 
                    <span><strong class="pop" style="color:blue" href="bibliography/Wb." title="eDIL Bibliography">Wb.</strong></span> 10c3

<script>

	  $(document).ready( function() {

	  	$('#content').on('click', '.pop', function() {
	  		$.ajax({
	            context: this,  // set the context of the callbacks
	            type: "GET",
	            url:  $(this).attr('href'),
	            success: function(data) {
	            	$(this).popover({
	            		placement: function (context, source) {
					        var position = $(source).position();
					        if (position.left > 515) {
					            return "left";
					        }
					        if (position.left < 515) {
					            return "right";
					        }
					        if (position.top < 110){
					            return "bottom";
					        }
					        return "top";
						},
				        content: data,
				        title: 'Bibliography',
				        html: true,
	            	}).popover('show');
	            }
        	});
	  	});

		$('body').on('click', function (e) {
            $('.pop').each(function () {
                //the 'is' for buttons that trigger popups
                //the 'has' for icons within a button that triggers a popup
                if (!$(this).is(e.target) && $(this).has(e.target).length === 0 && $('.popover').has(e.target).length === 0) {
                    $(this).popover('destroy');
                }
            });
        });
	  })
</script>

	.popover {
		max-width: 350px;
	}
